<p><b>Citi Field</b> is a stadium located in <a href="/wiki/Flushing_Meadows%E2%80%93Corona_Park" title="Flushing Meadows–Corona Park">Flushing Meadows–Corona Park</a> in the New York City borough of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>. Completed in <a href="/wiki/2009_in_baseball" title="2009 in baseball">2009</a>, it is the home <a href="/wiki/Baseball_park" title="Baseball park">baseball park</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>. Citi Field was built as a replacement for the formerly adjacent <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>, which opened in <a href="/wiki/1964_in_baseball" title="1964 in baseball">1964</a> next to the site of the <a href="/wiki/1964_New_York_World%27s_Fair" title="1964 New York World's Fair">1964–1965 World's Fair</a>. Citi Field was designed by <a href="/wiki/Populous_(company)" title="Populous (company)">Populous</a> (then HOK Sport), and is named after <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>, a New York financial services company which purchased the <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a>. The $850 million baseball park was funded with $615 million in public subsides,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> including the sale of New York City <a href="/wiki/Municipal_bond" title="Municipal bond">municipal bonds</a> which are to be repaid by the Mets plus interest. The payments will <a href="/wiki/Payment_in_lieu_of_taxes" title="Payment in lieu of taxes">offset property taxes</a> for the lifetime of the park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The Mets are receiving $20 million annually from Citibank in exchange for naming the stadium Citi Field. The entire public cost is being borne by city and state taxpayers in New York.</p>
<p>The first game at Citi Field was on March 29, 2009, with a <a href="/wiki/College_baseball" title="College baseball">college baseball</a> game between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Red_Storm_baseball" title="St. John's Red Storm baseball">St. John's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Hoyas" title="Georgetown Hoyas">Georgetown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The Mets played their first two games at the ballpark on April 3 and April 4, <a href="/wiki/2009_in_baseball" title="2009 in baseball">2009</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2009_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2009 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> as charity exhibition games. The first regular season home game was played on April 13, <a href="/wiki/2009_in_baseball" title="2009 in baseball">2009</a>, against the <a href="/wiki/2009_San_Diego_Padres_season" title="2009 San Diego Padres season">San Diego Padres</a>. Citi Field hosted the <a href="/wiki/2013_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2013 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2013 Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a>. This marked the second time the Mets have hosted the game, the first being <a href="/wiki/1964_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="1964 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">1964</a>, the inaugural season of Shea Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning">Planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the 1990s, the Mets had been looking to replace Shea Stadium. It had originally been built as a <a href="/wiki/Multi-purpose_stadium" title="Multi-purpose stadium">multi-purpose stadium</a> in 1964. While it had been retrofitted as a baseball-only stadium after the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> left for <a href="/wiki/Giants_Stadium" title="Giants Stadium">Giants Stadium</a> after the 1983 season, it was still not optimized for baseball, with seating located farther away from the playing field compared to other major league ballparks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The team unveiled a preliminary model of the ballpark in 1998; it featured a <a href="/wiki/Retractable_roof" title="Retractable roof">retractable roof</a> and a movable grass field, which would have allowed it to host events including conventions and college basketball. The Mets also considered moving to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitchel_Field" title="Mitchel Field">Mitchel Field</a> or <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Park" title="Belmont Park">Belmont Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_New_York" title="Nassau County, New York">Nassau County</a>, Long Island; <a href="/wiki/Sunnyside_Yard" title="Sunnyside Yard">Sunnyside Yard</a> in Queens, or the <a href="/wiki/West_Side_Yard" title="West Side Yard">West Side Yard</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roof_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-roof-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2001, shortly before leaving office, New York City <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_New_York_City" title="Mayor of New York City">Mayor</a> <a href="/wiki/Rudy_Giuliani" title="Rudy Giuliani">Rudy Giuliani</a> announced "tentative agreements" for both the Mets and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> to build new stadiums. Of the $1.6 billion sought for the stadiums, city and state taxpayers would pick up half the tab for construction, $800 million, along with $390 million on extra transportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bballeditorial_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-bballeditorial-16">[16]</a></sup> The plan also said that the teams would be allowed to keep all parking revenues, which state officials had already said they wanted to keep to compensate the state for building new garages for the teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloombergnytimes_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloombergnytimes-17">[17]</a></sup> The teams would keep 96% of ticket revenues and 100% of all other revenues, not pay sales tax or property tax on the stadium, and would get low-cost electricity from New York state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloombergnytimes_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloombergnytimes-17">[17]</a></sup> Business officials criticized the plan as giving too much money to successful teams with little reason to move to a different city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloombergnytimes_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-bloombergnytimes-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Bloomberg" title="Michael Bloomberg">Michael Bloomberg</a>, who succeeded Giuliani as mayor, exercised the <a href="/wiki/Escape_clause" title="Escape clause">escape clause</a> in the agreements to back out of both deals, saying that the city could not afford to build new stadiums for the Mets and Yankees. Bloomberg said that unbeknownst to him, Giuliani had inserted a clause in this deal which loosened the teams' leases with the city and would allow the Mets and Yankees to leave the city on 60 days' notice to find a new home elsewhere if the city backed out of the agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bballeditorial_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-bballeditorial-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloombergnytimes_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-bloombergnytimes-17">[17]</a></sup> At the time, Bloomberg said that publicly funded stadiums were a poor investment. Under Bloomberg, the New York City government would only offer public financing for infrastructure improvements; the teams would have to pay for the stadiums themselves. Bloomberg called the former mayor's agreements "<a href="/wiki/Corporate_welfare" title="Corporate welfare">corporate welfare</a>." Giuliani had already been instrumental in the construction of taxpayer-funded minor league baseball facilities <a href="/wiki/MCU_Park" title="MCU Park">MCU Park</a> for the Mets' minor league <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Cyclones" title="Brooklyn Cyclones">Brooklyn Cyclones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richmond_County_Bank_Ballpark" title="Richmond County Bank Ballpark">Richmond County Bank Ballpark</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island_Yankees" title="Staten Island Yankees">Staten Island Yankees</a>.</p>
<p>The final plans for what is now Citi Field were created as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_2012_Olympic_bid" title="New York City 2012 Olympic bid">New York City 2012 Olympic bid</a>. After plans for a <a href="/wiki/West_Side_Stadium" title="West Side Stadium">West Side Stadium</a> fell through, New York looked for an alternate stadium to host the opening and closing ceremonies and track and field. The Olympic Stadium project on the West Side was estimated to cost $2.2 billion, with $300 million provided by New York City and an additional $300 million from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York State</a>. If New York had won the bid, Citi Field would have been expanded to Olympic events while the Mets would have played at <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a> in the Bronx for the 2012 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="648" data-file-width="972" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg/220px-Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg/330px-Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg/440px-Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_Construction_9-14-07.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Citi Field under construction on September 14, 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The projected cost of the new ballpark and other infrastructure improvements is $610 million, with the Mets picking up $420 million of that amount. The agreement includes a 40-year lease that will keep the Mets in New York until 2049. The Mets own the stadium through a wholly owned subsidiary, Queens Ballpark Company.</p>
<p>On March 18, 2006, the New York Mets unveiled the official model for the new ballpark. By July 2006, initial construction of the new park was underway in the parking lot beyond Shea Stadium's left-field, with a projected finish ahead of <a href="/wiki/Opening_Day" title="Opening Day">Opening Day</a> 2009 in late March.</p>
<p>By April 13, 2008, all of the structure for the Jackie Robinson Rotunda was in place with the arched windows receiving their paneling and glass. By September 2008, most of the Citi Field signage had been installed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> By December 1, 2008, all of the seats and the playing field had been installed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modifications">Modifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 2010 offseason, the <a href="/wiki/Bullpen" title="Bullpen">bullpen</a> area in right-center field underwent a complete renovation. When the edifice opened in time for the start of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_MLB_season" title="2009 MLB season">2009 MLB season</a>, the Mets' bullpen was in front of the visiting bullpen, leading to an obstructed view of the field from the visiting bullpen, which the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> complained about during the Mets' first regular-season home series. The bullpens were turned 90°, with pitchers throwing toward the field instead of parallel to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> More Mets team colors, player banners and logos were also added throughout the ballpark, including revamping the "Let's Go Mets" slogan on the Citi Vision board so that the word "Mets" appears in its traditional script instead of the same font as the rest of the slogan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Mets_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Mets-22">[22]</a></sup> Additionally, the height of the home run boundary line directly in front of the Home Run Apple in center field was reduced from 16 feet (4.9 m) to 8 feet (2.4 m) in an attempt to produce more home runs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changes_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-changes-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>During its first three seasons, the large field dimensions caused Citi Field to play as an extreme "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_baseball_jargon_(P)#pitcher.27s_park" title="List of baseball jargon (P)">pitcher's park</a>", and home-runs at the stadium were among the fewest in the Major Leagues. Mets' general manager <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Alderson" title="Sandy Alderson">Sandy Alderson</a> changed Citi Field's dimensions in time for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_MLB_season" title="2012 MLB season">2012 MLB season</a> in order to make it more friendly to hitters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Changes include building an 8 feet (2.4 m) wall in front of the high 16 feet (4.9 m) wall in left field that many had dubbed the "Great Wall of Flushing", removing the nook in the "<a href="/wiki/Modell%27s" title="Modell's">Mo's</a> Zone" in right field, and reducing the distance in right center field from 415 feet (126 m) from home plate to 390 feet (120 m). The new walls are colored blue in order to address fan complaints that the old black walls with orange trims did not reflect the colors of the Mets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changes_2_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-changes_2-25">[25]</a></sup> The Mets have also created a new seating section located in between the old and new left field walls called the <a href="/wiki/Party_City" title="Party City">Party City</a> Deck and can accommodate 102 additional fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Party_City_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Party_City-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The center and right-center outfield wall were brought in to 380 feet (120 m) for the 2015 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1972" data-file-width="3264" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG/220px-Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG/330px-Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG/440px-Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_and_Apple.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Entrance to Citi Field through the <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> Rotunda, with Shea Stadium's Home Run Apple on the right.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Citi Field has a capacity of 41,922. It has over 15,000 fewer seats than Shea Stadium. All the seats in the park are green – in an homage to the <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a>, longtime home of the baseball Giants and the original home of the Mets – as opposed to Shea's orange, blue, red and green assortment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews.com_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews.com-27">[27]</a></sup> The exterior facade is reminiscent of <a href="/wiki/Ebbets_Field" title="Ebbets Field">Ebbets Field</a> (which was long sought by Mets owner <a href="/wiki/Fred_Wilpon" title="Fred Wilpon">Fred Wilpon</a>, a Brooklyn native).</p>
<p>Citi Field's interior design is primarily influenced by <a href="/wiki/PNC_Park" title="PNC Park">PNC Park</a>, which was the favorite ballpark of Mets COO <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Wilpon" title="Jeff Wilpon">Jeff Wilpon</a>. Other influences include <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Ball_Park" title="Great American Ball Park">Great American Ball Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coors_Field" title="Coors Field">Coors Field</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Bank_Park" title="Citizens Bank Park">Citizens Bank Park</a>. Shea Stadium was the only ballpark in the Major Leagues to feature orange <a href="/wiki/Baseball_field#Foul_poles" title="Baseball field">foul poles</a> instead of the standard yellow, a unique characteristic that made its way into Citi Field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lupica_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lupica-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shea_Bridge_2012.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="709" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Shea_Bridge_2012.png/220px-Shea_Bridge_2012.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Shea_Bridge_2012.png/330px-Shea_Bridge_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Shea_Bridge_2012.png/440px-Shea_Bridge_2012.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shea_Bridge_2012.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shea Bridge</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Citi Field features an overarching bridge motif in its architecture, as New York City is linked by 2,027 bridges and is reflected in the Mets logo, as the team is the symbolic bridge to the city's past National League teams, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_Giants_(NL)" title="History of the New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="History of the Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews.com_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews.com-27">[27]</a></sup> In the outfield section of the ballpark, there is a pedestrian bridge named Shea Bridge which resembles the <a href="/wiki/Hell_Gate_Bridge" title="Hell Gate Bridge">Hell Gate Bridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Mets_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Mets-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Similar to Shea Stadium, Citi Field's field dimensions make it a pitcher friendly park. The <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> Corner, originally known as the <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> Porch, hangs over the field in right field, extending far beyond the indentation of the Clubhouse and is inspired by <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Stadium_(Detroit)" title="Tiger Stadium (Detroit)">Tiger Stadium</a>'s right field porch. The Pepsi sign that sat atop the area (2009-2015) was modeled after the one alongside the <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">East River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gantry_Plaza_State_Park" title="Gantry Plaza State Park">Gantry Plaza State Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012 The Mets added the Party City Party Deck in left field because they moved the fences in. The Party Deck is very similar to The Royals Pepsi Party Porch.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> signed a multiyear deal on September 15, 2008, to sponsor an exclusive section in Citi Field. The Delta Sky360 Club is a 22,500-square-foot (2,090 m<sup>2</sup>) restaurant-cafe-bar-lounge complex that also houses 1,600 premium seats behind home plate stretching from dugout to dugout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt2009-03-24_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt2009-03-24-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda">Jackie Robinson Rotunda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Jackie Robinson Rotunda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg/220px-Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg/330px-Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg/440px-Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jackie_Robinson_Rotunda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The interior of the Jackie Robinson Rotunda</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The front entrance of Citi Field features a rotunda named after Brooklyn Dodgers legend <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> and honors his life and accomplishments. Engraved into the rotunda's 160-foot-diameter (49 m) floor and etched into the archways are words and larger-than-life images that defined Robinson's nine values: Courage, Excellence, Persistence, Justice, Teamwork, Commitment, Citizenship, Determination and Integrity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lupica_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lupica-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Robinson's famous quote: "A life is not important except in the impact it has on other lives", is engraved into the upper ring of the rotunda. There is also an 8-foot (2.4 m) sculpture of Robinson's number 42.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews.com_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews.com-27">[27]</a></sup> The formal dedication of the Jackie Robinson Rotunda was held as part of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>'s official celebration of <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson_Day" title="Jackie Robinson Day">Jackie Robinson Day</a> on April 15, <a href="/wiki/2009_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2009 Major League Baseball season">2009</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_Run_Apples">Home Run Apples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Home Run Apples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1122" data-file-width="1092" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg/170px-Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg/255px-Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg/340px-Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_Home_Run_Apple_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Citi Field's Home Run Apple located in center field.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another tradition from Shea Stadium making an appearance in Citi Field is the Home Run Apple. When a Mets player hits a home run, a giant apple, which has a Mets logo on the front that lights up, rises from its housing in the center field batter's eye. The new apple that has been constructed for Citi Field is more than four times the size of the previous one and was designed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis</a>-based engineering firm <a href="/wiki/Uni-Systems" title="Uni-Systems">Uni-Systems</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Shea's original apple was located inside Citi Field's bullpen entrance gate for the 2009 season. In 2010, the Shea apple was relocated outside the ballpark at Mets Plaza, in between the Jackie Robinson Rotunda and the entrance to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mets_%E2%80%93_Willets_Point_(IRT_Flushing_Line)" title="Mets – Willets Point (IRT Flushing Line)">Mets–Willets Point</a> subway station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Amenities_and_facilities">Amenities and facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Amenities and facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Behind the center field scoreboard is the FanFest area, an expanded family entertainment area that includes a miniature <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wiffleball" title="Wiffleball">wiffleball</a> field replica of Citi Field called <a href="/wiki/Mr._Met" title="Mr. Met">Mr. Met</a>'s Kiddie Field, a batting cage, a dunk tank, video game kiosks and other attractions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Citi Field offers a wide choice of eateries. Taste of the City is a food court located in the center field section of the ballpark. It features food from restaurateur <a href="/wiki/Danny_Meyer" title="Danny Meyer">Danny Meyer</a>'s Union Square Hospitality Group and includes a variety of stands, including <a href="/wiki/Shake_Shack" title="Shake Shack">Shake Shack</a> (burgers, fries, shakes), Blue Smoke (barbecue), El Verano Taqueria (Mexican cuisine), Catch of the Day (featuring seafood from chef Dave Pasternack of Esca) and Box Frites (Belgian French fries).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews.com_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews.com-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nym-2010-03-24_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-nym-2010-03-24-36">[36]</a></sup> The World's Fare Market is located on the field level in right field and features sushi from Daruma of Tokyo, sandwiches and pastries from Mama's of Corona, Chinese cuisine from Tai Pan Bakery and Korean food from Café Hanover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nym-2010-03-24_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-nym-2010-03-24-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Citi Field also offers a choice of fresh fruit at several stands around the stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In 2010 Citi Field upgraded the food choices on the Promenade Level behind home plate. Blue Smoke BBQ and Box Frites both open a second location.</p>
<p>Restaurants and clubs are also available in every level of the ballpark. The 350-seat Acela Club, located in left field on the Excelsior Level, is the dining highlight of the new park and features a full view of the playing field as well as food from <a href="/wiki/Drew_Nieporent" title="Drew Nieporent">Drew Nieporent</a>'s Myriad Restaurant Group, renowned for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobu" title="Nobu">Nobu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Grill" title="Tribeca Grill">Tribeca Grill</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nydailynews.com_27-4"><a href="#cite_note-nydailynews.com-27">[27]</a></sup> Admission into the high-end luxury Acela and Delta clubs, and including the other semi-luxury clubs are exclusive to high-end ticket holders only, and some restaurants enforce that reservations be made. A McFadden's Restaurant and Saloon opened at Citi Field in 2010. It is located directly under the 2K Sports FanFest and is open to the public year-round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mets_Hall_of_Fame_.26_Museum">Mets Hall of Fame &amp; Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mets Hall of Fame &amp; Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Original_Mr._Met.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2730" data-file-width="2400" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Original_Mr._Met.JPG/170px-Original_Mr._Met.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Original_Mr._Met.JPG/255px-Original_Mr._Met.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Original_Mr._Met.JPG/340px-Original_Mr._Met.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Original_Mr._Met.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The original <a href="/wiki/Mr._Met" title="Mr. Met">Mr. Met</a> costume is one of the many exhibits on display at the Mets Hall of Fame and Museum.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg/220px-David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg/330px-David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg/440px-David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Cone_19-K_game_jersey.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/David_Cone" title="David Cone">David Cone</a>'s jersey from his 19 <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeout</a> game on October 6, 1991, housed in the Mets Hall of Fame and Museum</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mets Hall of Fame &amp; Museum is located adjacent to the Jackie Robinson Rotunda on the first base side and opened on April 5, 2010. The museum includes plaques honoring the inductees of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets_Hall_of_Fame" title="New York Mets Hall of Fame">New York Mets Hall of Fame</a>, the team's <a href="/wiki/Commissioner%27s_Trophy_(MLB)" title="Commissioner's Trophy (MLB)">World Series trophies</a> from <a href="/wiki/1969_World_Series" title="1969 World Series">1969</a> and <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Series" title="1986 World Series">1986</a>, as well as artifacts on loan from noted collectors, former players and the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The museum boasts several displays including autographed memorabilia, original scouting reports on players such as Darryl Strawberry, and handwritten notes from the team's first manager <a href="/wiki/Casey_Stengel" title="Casey Stengel">Casey Stengel</a>. In addition to this the team has installed interactive touchscreens that guide visitors through various aspects of the franchise's 50-year history, and there are television screens and timelines that help weave all the disparate elements into a cohesive narrative.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:QueensMinorLeagueGame.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="273" data-file-width="365" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/70/QueensMinorLeagueGame.JPG/200px-QueensMinorLeagueGame.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/70/QueensMinorLeagueGame.JPG/300px-QueensMinorLeagueGame.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/70/QueensMinorLeagueGame.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:QueensMinorLeagueGame.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The ballpark has also been used for amateur baseball games on TV and in movies.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i> praised the stadium for its aesthetics and named it one of the top 100 venues in sports, while BaseballParks.com called it "perfect" and especially lauded the Jackie Robinson Rotunda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Reviewers have also praised the many culinary offerings at Citi Field's concession stands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the modern amenities, Citi Field has not been without criticism. Most notable have been fan complaints of obstructed views, as well as Mets fans' outrage at overemphasis on the celebration of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="History of the Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a>' legacy over the history of the Mets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Mets owner <a href="/wiki/Fred_Wilpon" title="Fred Wilpon">Fred Wilpon</a>, a Brooklyn native, had grown up a Brooklyn Dodgers fan and admitted to going overboard; <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Toobin" title="Jeffrey Toobin">Jeffrey Toobin</a> wrote in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i>,</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">When Citi Field opened, the Brooklyn focus drew some criticism. After all, the Dodgers left Brooklyn in 1957, and Ebbets Field was demolished shortly thereafter. Only the very oldest fans have any first-hand memory of the place. The Mets, who had been in existence for almost a half century, were virtually ignored in their own home. 'All the Dodger stuff—that was an error of judgment on my part,' Wilpon told me.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2184" data-file-width="3264" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg/220px-5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg/330px-5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg/440px-5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:5.9.14CitiFieldControlRoomByLuigiNovi5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The control room on the fifth level Concourse.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In response to these criticisms, the team installed photographic imagery of famous players and historic moments in Mets history on the Field and Promenade levels as well as the display of team championship banners on the left-field wall during the 2009 season. They also constructed a Mets Hall of Fame and Museum prior to the 2010 season, located adjacent to the Jackie Robinson Rotunda, and changed the color of the outfield wall from black to Mets blue prior to the 2012 season, which many Mets fans had campaigned for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The team also worked on fixing the obstructed views in the Promenade level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>During its first three seasons in existence, Citi Field was known to play as a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_baseball_jargon_(P)#pitcher.27s_park" title="List of baseball jargon (P)">pitcher's park</a>", and has been cited as the cause of the decreased offensive production of <a href="/wiki/David_Wright" title="David Wright">David Wright</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Bay" title="Jason Bay">Jason Bay</a>. Wright hit only 10 home runs in 2009 after hitting at least 30 in the previous two seasons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> while Bay had the worst offensive production of his career in his first season with the Mets in 2010, only hitting 6 home runs, 47 RBIs, and OBP of just .347, and a slugging percentage of a career low .402.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Francoeur" title="Jeff Francoeur">Jeff Francoeur</a>, who played with the Mets during their first two years at Citi Field, criticized the ballpark's dimensions, calling it "a damn joke."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> During the 2011 season, Citi Field allowed 1.33 home runs per game, the third lowest total out of the 16 National League ballparks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changes_2_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-changes_2-25">[25]</a></sup> The team responded by altering the ballpark dimensions for the 2012 season, creating a more neutral ballpark. Wright's 2012 offensive numbers have improved due to the alterations. "It's a huge difference", Wright said. "It allows you to relax and know you don’t have to try to hit the ball a mile to see results. And at the same time, if you do hit the ball well and you see results, instead of a 400-foot flyout, you’re 1-for-1 and feeling good about yourself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Access_and_transportation">Access and transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Access and transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MetsCiti.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/MetsCiti.jpg/220px-MetsCiti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/MetsCiti.jpg/330px-MetsCiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/MetsCiti.jpg/440px-MetsCiti.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MetsCiti.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Citi Field is serviced by the <a href="/wiki/IRT_Flushing_Line" title="IRT Flushing Line">IRT Flushing Line</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mets_%E2%80%93_Willets_Point_(IRT_Flushing_Line)" title="Mets – Willets Point (IRT Flushing Line)">Mets – Willets Point</a> station.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Citi Field is located in the borough of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, adjacent to the neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Corona,_Queens" title="Corona, Queens">Corona</a>, which lies to its west, and <a href="/wiki/Willets_Point,_Queens" title="Willets Point, Queens">Willets Point</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flushing,_Queens" title="Flushing, Queens">Flushing</a> to the east. <a href="/wiki/Flushing_Bay" title="Flushing Bay">Flushing Bay</a> is to the north, and the rest of <a href="/wiki/Flushing_Meadows%E2%80%93Corona_Park" title="Flushing Meadows–Corona Park">Flushing Meadows–Corona Park</a> is to the south. Because it lies within the Flushing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZIP_code#ZIP_codes_only_loosely_tied_to_cities" title="ZIP code">postal zone</a>, and because of its location in Flushing Meadows–Corona Park, Citi Field is frequently referred to as being in Flushing proper.</p>
<p>Citi Field is accessible via mass transit systems such as the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a> via the <a href="/wiki/IRT_Flushing_Line" title="IRT Flushing Line">IRT Flushing Line</a> (<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/7_(New_York_City_Subway_service)" title="7 (New York City Subway service)">7</a></span> <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7d_(New_York_City_Subway_service)" title="7d (New York City Subway service)">&lt;7&gt;</a></span> trains) at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mets_%E2%80%93_Willets_Point_(IRT_Flushing_Line)" title="Mets – Willets Point (IRT Flushing Line)">Mets – Willets Point</a> station, and the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Rail_Road" title="Long Island Rail Road">Long Island Rail Road</a> station on the <a href="/wiki/Port_Washington_Branch" title="Port Washington Branch">Port Washington Branch</a> also called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mets_%E2%80%93_Willets_Point_(LIRR_station)" title="Mets – Willets Point (LIRR station)">Mets – Willets Point</a>. <a href="/wiki/New_York_Water_Taxi" title="New York Water Taxi">New York Water Taxi</a> operates a free ferry to the stadium from <a href="/wiki/Pier_11/Wall_Street" title="Pier 11/Wall Street">Pier 11/Wall Street</a> and the <a href="/wiki/East_34th_Street_Ferry_Landing" title="East 34th Street Ferry Landing">East 34th Street Ferry Landing</a> before every game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> For selected games, <a href="/wiki/SeaStreak" title="SeaStreak">SeaStreak</a> provides ferry service between <a href="/wiki/Highlands,_New_Jersey" title="Highlands, New Jersey">Highlands, New Jersey</a> and the stadium. Both ferry services use the slips at the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair_Marina" title="World's Fair Marina">World's Fair Marina</a>, located approximately 0.25 miles (0.40 km) north of Citi Field. The park is also close to several major thoroughfares, including the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Parkway" title="Grand Central Parkway">Grand Central Parkway</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_678_(New_York)" title="Interstate 678 (New York)">Whitestone and Van Wyck Expressways</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(New_York)" title="Interstate 495 (New York)">Long Island Expressway</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Avenue" title="Roosevelt Avenue">Roosevelt Avenue</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Route_25A" title="New York State Route 25A">Northern Boulevard</a> and Astoria Boulevard.</p>
<p>Citi Field is near to the <a href="/wiki/USTA_Billie_Jean_King_National_Tennis_Center" title="USTA Billie Jean King National Tennis Center">USTA Billie Jean King National Tennis Center</a>, where the annual <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a> grand-slam tennis tournament is held.</p>
<p>Since the construction of Citi Field began, satellite parking lots in Flushing Meadow Park (access from College Point Boulevard) have been opened.</p>
<div style="clear:right;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Attendance_records">Attendance records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Attendance records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regular_Season">Regular Season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Regular Season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Bold</b> indicates the winner of each game.</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">
<tr>
<td colspan="5" style="background:#002D72;color:#FFFFFF"><b>Highest regular season attendance at Citi Field</b></td>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming_rights">Naming rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Naming rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On November 13, 2006, it was officially announced that the ballpark would be called Citi Field, named for <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup Inc</a>. Citigroup will be paying $20 million a year for the <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a> to the park over the next 20 years. This made Citi Field the second major league sports venue in the area named for a corporate sponsor, (after <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a> Arena (now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Izod_Center" title="Izod Center">Izod Center</a>)), but preceding <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Center" title="Prudential Center">Prudential Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Arena_(New_Jersey)" title="Red Bull Arena (New Jersey)">Red Bull Arena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a>, officially becoming the first in New York City itself, aside from two minor league ballparks (<a href="/wiki/MCU_Park" title="MCU Park">MCU Park</a> in Brooklyn, and <a href="/wiki/Richmond_County_Bank_Ballpark" title="Richmond County Bank Ballpark">Richmond County Bank Ballpark</a> in <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a>). The deal includes an option on both sides to extend the contract to 40 years, and is the most expensive sports-stadium naming rights agreement ever, subsequently equaled by MetLife Stadium's $400 million deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the groundbreaking for Citi Field, it was announced that the main entrance, modeled on the one in Brooklyn's old Ebbets Field, would be called the <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> Rotunda, possibly due to campaigns to forgo naming rights revenue and name the ballpark after Robinson. The Mets are spending more than $600 million for the new ballpark, which New York City and New York state are also supporting with a total of $165 million for such costs as infrastructure and site preparation. On February 24, 2008, the Mets and Citigroup unveiled the new Citi Field logo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2427" data-file-width="2994" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG/220px-Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG/330px-Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG/440px-Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jonathan_Lethem_Occupy_Wall_Street_2011_Shankbone.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Lethem" title="Jonathan Lethem">Jonathan Lethem</a> at <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> protesting the naming rights given to <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>, November 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Both Citigroup<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and the Mets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> maintain that the naming rights deal is secure, despite Citigroup's economic troubles. This deal has been criticized in light of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-2000s_financial_crisis" title="Late-2000s financial crisis">late-2000s financial crisis</a> and the $45 billion of taxpayer funds allocated to Citigroup by the U.S. federal government in two separate rescue packages, prompting <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Council" title="New York City Council">New York City Council</a> members <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vincent_Ignizio" title="Vincent Ignizio">Vincent Ignizio</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Oddo" title="James Oddo">James Oddo</a> to suggest that the new ballpark be called "Citi/Taxpayer Field." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Radio talk show host <a href="/wiki/Brian_Lehrer" title="Brian Lehrer">Brian Lehrer</a> suggested the name "Debits Field" which combines baseball history with public outrage over the Citi bailout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Congressman <a href="/wiki/Elijah_Cummings" title="Elijah Cummings">Elijah Cummings</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, who serves on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Committee_on_Oversight_and_Government_Reform" title="United States House Committee on Oversight and Government Reform">United States House Committee on Oversight and Government Reform</a>, stated in regards to the Citi Field naming rights deal, "This type of spending is indefensible and unacceptable to Citigroup's new partner and largest investor: the American taxpayer.... I strongly urge Citigroup to find a way out of this contract and instead spend that $400 million on retaining its employees and restoring confidence in its operations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On January 29, 2009, congressmen <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Kucinich" title="Dennis Kucinich">Dennis Kucinich</a> of Ohio and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Poe" title="Ted Poe">Ted Poe</a> of Texas sent a letter to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">United States Secretary of the Treasury</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timothy_F._Geithner" title="Timothy F. Geithner">Timothy F. Geithner</a> urging him to scrap Citigroup's $400 million naming rights deal. "We request that you intervene and demand that Citigroup dissolve the agreement they have with the New York Mets", reads the letter. "Absent this outcome, we feel strongly that you should compel Citigroup to return immediately all federal monies received to date, as well as cancel all loan guarantees."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> However, Geithner rejected congressional demands to cancel the naming rights deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> reported on February 3, 2009, that Citigroup considered breaking the naming rights deal. Citi has stated that no government <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Troubled_Assets_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Assets Relief Program">TARP</a> funds would be used in the sponsorship deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The naming rights controversy reemerged when details about owner Fred Wilpon's involvement in <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Madoff" title="Bernard Madoff">Bernard Madoff</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ponzi_scheme" title="Ponzi scheme">Ponzi scheme</a> came to light when a lawsuit was filed on behalf of victims of <a href="/wiki/Madoff_investment_scandal" title="Madoff investment scandal">Madoff's investment scandal</a> in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium_comparison">Stadium comparison</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Stadium comparison">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_Day.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Citi_Field_Day.jpg/220px-Citi_Field_Day.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Citi_Field_Day.jpg/330px-Citi_Field_Day.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Citi_Field_Day.jpg/440px-Citi_Field_Day.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_Day.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In its opening season, Citi Field drew over 3.1 million fans with a game average of 92.7% of seats filled, 4th best in baseball.</div>
</div>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_events">Notable events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>April 13, 2009 – In the first Mets game ever played at Citi Field, <a href="/wiki/Jody_Gerut" title="Jody Gerut">Jody Gerut</a> of the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> hit a home run off <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pelfrey" title="Mike Pelfrey">Mike Pelfrey</a> as the first batter of the game, becoming the first player in Major League Baseball history to open a ballpark with a leadoff home run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li>April 17, 2009 – <a href="/wiki/Gary_Sheffield" title="Gary Sheffield">Gary Sheffield</a> hit his <a href="/wiki/500_home_run_club" title="500 home run club">500th home run</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a>, becoming the first player to reach this milestone as a pinch hitter. It was Sheffield's first home run as a Met, which made Sheffield the first player to hit number 500 as his first home run with a new team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li>June 28, 2009 – <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rivera" title="Mariano Rivera">Mariano Rivera</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> recorded his 500th career save, becoming only the second relief pitcher to reach this milestone. The Mets gave Rivera the pitching rubber from Citi Field used in the game in honor of his achievement. (Rivera's only <a href="/wiki/Run_batted_in" title="Run batted in">RBI</a>, on a bases-loaded walk, also occurred in the game.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 11, 2011 – Citi Field hosted a <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Night_Baseball" title="Sunday Night Baseball">nationally televised</a> game against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> to mark the tenth anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">attacks of that day in 2001</a>. The pregame ceremonies featured members of the 2001 team who played at Shea Stadium on September 21, 2001, the first major sporting event held in New York City since the attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>June 1, 2012 – <a href="/wiki/Johan_Santana" title="Johan Santana">Johan Santana</a> threw the first <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitter</a> in Mets franchise history in a 8-0 victory over the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, ending a 50-year drought, the longest in Major League Baseball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 16, 2013 – Citi Field hosted the <a href="/wiki/2013_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2013 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2013 Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a>, with the American League defeating the National League 3-0. The attendance of 45,186 was the largest in Citi Field's history.</li>
<li>June 9, 2015 – <a href="/wiki/Chris_Heston" title="Chris Heston">Chris Heston</a> of the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> threw a no-hitter in a 5-0 victory over the Mets.</li>
<li>October 3, 2015 – <a href="/wiki/Max_Scherzer" title="Max Scherzer">Max Scherzer</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> threw a no-hitter in a 2-0 victory over the Mets, becoming the fifth pitcher in major league history to throw two no hitters in a season.</li>
<li>October 12, 2015 – Citi Field hosted its first playoff game, with the Mets defeating the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> 13-7 in Game 3 of the <a href="/wiki/2015_National_League_Division_Series" title="2015 National League Division Series">2015 NLDS</a>.</li>
<li>October 30, 2015 – Citi Field hosted its first <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> game, with the Mets defeating the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> 9-3 in Game 3 of the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015 World Series</a>.</li>
<li>November 1, 2015 – The Kansas City Royals won the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015 World Series</a>, their first World Series championship since the <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">1985 World Series</a> with a 7-2 Game 5 victory over the Mets in 12 innings.</li>
<li>July 30, 2016 - In a pre-game ceremony before a 7-2 loss to the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Piazza" title="Mike Piazza">Mike Piazza</a>'s #31 was retired, only the second time in club history that the Mets retired a player's number.</li>
<li>October 5, 2016 - The San Francisco Giants defeated the Mets 3-0 in the <a href="/wiki/2016_National_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2016 National League Wild Card Game">2016 National League Wild Card Game</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_events">Other events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> performed <a href="/wiki/Good_Evening_New_York_City" title="Good Evening New York City">a series of three sold-out concerts</a> at Citi Field on July 17, 18 and 21, 2009 as a part of his <a href="/wiki/Summer_Live_%2709" title="Summer Live '09">Summer Live '09</a> tour, along with <a href="/wiki/The_Script" title="The Script">The Script</a>. McCartney, as a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, performed in the first concert at Shea Stadium during their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_1965_U.S._tour" title="The Beatles' 1965 U.S. tour">1965 U.S. Tour</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_1966_U.S._tour" title="The Beatles' 1966 U.S. tour">The Beatles' 1966 U.S. tour</a> as well as in its final concert in 2008 along with <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">Billy Joel</a>, who came out on McCartney's first night for the Beatles' classic, "<a href="/wiki/I_Saw_Her_Standing_There" title="I Saw Her Standing There">I Saw Her Standing There</a>." McCartney's opening show would later be released as <a href="/wiki/Good_Evening_New_York_City" title="Good Evening New York City">Good Evening New York City</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dave_Matthews_Band" title="Dave Matthews Band">Dave Matthews Band</a> performed two concerts at Citi Field on July 16 and 17, 2010, along with the <a href="/wiki/Zac_Brown_Band" title="Zac Brown Band">Zac Brown Band</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The second night was later released as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_in_New_York_City_(Dave_Matthews_Band)" title="Live in New York City (Dave Matthews Band)">Live in New York City</a>.</p>
<p>The documentary film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_Play_at_Shea" title="Last Play at Shea">Last Play at Shea</a></i>, chronicling Billy Joel's final concert at Shea Stadium in 2008, premiered on August 21, 2010, at Citi Field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 7, 2011, Citi Field hosted its first <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> game. The game was a friendly match between the national teams of <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a>, who played to a 1–1 tie, before a crowd of 39,656. The success of the game has led the Mets to consider having Citi Field host future soccer games as well as the <a href="/wiki/NHL_Winter_Classic" title="NHL Winter Classic">NHL Winter Classic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Citi Field hosted another soccer match on July 26, 2011, between the Italian team <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus F.C.</a> and the Mexican <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club América">Club América</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Football_Challenge" title="2011 World Football Challenge">2011 World Football Challenge</a>. Juventus won the match 1–0, before a crowd of 20,859.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Ecuadorian national team returned to Citi Field to play against the <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">Chilean national team</a> in a soccer match on August 15, 2012. Ecuador won the match 3–0, before a crowd of 31,901.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> On June 2, 2013, the national teams of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_national_football_team" title="Israeli national football team">Israel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honduras_national_football_team" title="Honduras national football team">Honduras</a> faced off in a friendly, with Israel winning 2-0.</p>
<p>The inaugural Metropolitan Lacrosse Classic, only the second time a major-league baseball stadium has staged college lacrosse, according to the Mets. In 1971, Navy played Johns Hopkins at the Houston Astrodome. Holy Cross plays Navy at noon on Sunday, March 17, 2013, followed by Colgate-Michigan at 3 p.m.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Holy Cross defeated Navy 7–5 and Colgate defeated Michigan 10–7, before a crowd of 15,656.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 7, 2015, the first "Legends of Wrestling" event took place at Citi Field. It was a professional wrestling event, featuring veteran wrestlers such as <a href="/wiki/Rob_Van_Dam" title="Rob Van Dam">Rob Van Dam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lita_(wrestler)" title="Lita (wrestler)">Lita</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Nasty_Boys" title="The Nasty Boys">The Nasty Boys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Steiner" title="Scott Steiner">Scott Steiner</a>, and many more independent professional wrestlers, in up to six matches taking place; the event was headlined by <a href="/wiki/Ric_Flair" title="Ric Flair">Ric Flair</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bret_%22The_Hitman%22_Hart" title='Bret "The Hitman" Hart'>Bret "The Hitman" Hart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Goldberg" title="Bill Goldberg">Bill Goldberg</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a> played two concerts at Citi Field on July 15 and 16, 2015 as a part of their <a href="/wiki/Sonic_Highways_World_Tour" title="Sonic Highways World Tour">Sonic Highways World Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 7, 2015, Citi Field hosted the first game of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cricket_All-Stars_Series_2015" title="Cricket All-Stars Series 2015">Cricket All-Stars Series 2015</a>, featuring many retired <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> players from around the world and led by great cricket legends <a href="/wiki/Sachin_Tendulkar" title="Sachin Tendulkar">Sachin Tendulkar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shane_Warne" title="Shane Warne">Shane Warne</a>. Warne's Warriors defeated Sachin's Blasters by 6 wickets.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> performed at Citi Field on June 7 and 8, 2016, in front of a crowd of 73,486 people, as part of <a href="/wiki/The_Formation_World_Tour" title="The Formation World Tour">The Formation World Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Citi Field was featured in the <a href="/wiki/Curveball_(Ugly_Betty)" title="Curveball (Ugly Betty)">finale</a> of the third season of <a href="/wiki/Ugly_Betty" title="Ugly Betty">Ugly Betty</a>. Citi Field was also featured as a location in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Sharknado_2:_The_Second_One" title="Sharknado 2: The Second One">Sharknado 2: The Second One</a></i>, in which a tornado filled with sharks hits the ballpark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baseball_(crop).jpg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="1644" data-file-width="1697" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1e/Baseball_%28crop%29.jpg/29px-Baseball_%28crop%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1e/Baseball_%28crop%29.jpg/43px-Baseball_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1e/Baseball_%28crop%29.jpg/58px-Baseball_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" width="29"/></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Baseball" title="Portal:Baseball">Baseball portal</a></span></li>
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_York_City.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="500" height="19" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_New_York_City.svg/32px-Flag_of_New_York_City.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_New_York_City.svg/48px-Flag_of_New_York_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_New_York_City.svg/64px-Flag_of_New_York_City.svg.png 2x" width="32"/></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:New_York_City" title="Portal:New York City">New York City portal</a></span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>, the home of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">Mets</a> from 1964 to 2008</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a>, a baseball stadium in <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">The Bronx</a> for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>, which opened in April 2009</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prudential_Center" title="Prudential Center">Prudential Center</a>, an arena in <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark, New Jersey</a> for the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Devils" title="New Jersey Devils">New Jersey Devils</a>, which opened in October 2007</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a>, an arena in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Brooklyn Nets</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Islanders" title="New York Islanders">New York Islanders</a>, which opened in September 2012</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a>, a football stadium in <a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">East Rutherford, New Jersey</a> for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>, which opened in April 2010</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Arena_(Harrison)" title="Red Bull Arena (Harrison)">Red Bull Arena</a>, a soccer stadium in <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_New_Jersey" title="Harrison, New Jersey">Harrison, New Jersey</a> for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">New York Red Bulls</a>, which opened in March 2010</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Citi_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Mets lease the ballpark through a sub-company known as Queens Ballpark Company <a href="/wiki/Limited_liability_company" title="Limited liability company">LLC</a> (see <a class="external text" href="http://emma.msrb.org/EP632926-EP495302-EP896109.pdf" rel="nofollow">Queens Ballpark Company financial report</a>). That's because the land the ballpark was built on is owned by New York City and is leased to the Queens Ballpark Company, a division of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>. The company is in charge of managing the lease and making sure it is paid on time each year.</span></li>
